      <p>
       <b>
        Senegal
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">
            ˌ
           </span>
           <span title="'s' in 'sigh'">
            s
           </span>
           <span title="/ɛ/: 'e' in 'dress'">
            ɛ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">
            ɡ
           </span>
           <span title="/ɔː/: 'au' in 'fraud'">
            ɔː
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
          </span>
          , -
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">
            ɡ
           </span>
           <span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">
            ɑː
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="nowrap">
         (
         <span class="unicode haudio">
          <span class="fn">
           <span style="white-space:nowrap">
            <a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Senegal.ogg" title="About this sound">
             <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
            </a>
           </span>
           <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c1/En-us-Senegal.ogg" title="En-us-Senegal.ogg">
            listen
           </a>
          </span>
         </span>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       French:
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         Sénégal
        </span>
       </i>
       <span style="margin-left:2px">
        )
       </span>
       , officially the
       <b>
        Republic of Senegal
       </b>
       (French:
       <i>
        <span lang="fr">
         République du Sénégal
        </span>
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">
         [ʁepyblik dy seneɡal]
        </a>
       </span>
       ), is a country in
       <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">
        West Africa
       </a>
       . Senegal is bordered by
       <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">
        Mauritania
       </a>
       in the north,
       <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">
        Mali
       </a>
       to the east,
       <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">
        Guinea
       </a>
       to the southeast, and
       <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">
        Guinea-Bissau
       </a>
       to the southwest. Senegal also borders
       <a href="/wiki/The_Gambia" title="The Gambia">
        The Gambia
       </a>
       , a country occupying a narrow sliver of land along the banks of the
       <a href="/wiki/Gambia_River" title="Gambia River">
        Gambia River
       </a>
       , which separates Senegal's southern region of
       <a href="/wiki/Casamance" title="Casamance">
        Casamance
       </a>
       from the rest of the country. Senegal also shares a maritime border with
       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">
        Cape Verde
       </a>
       . Senegal's economic and political capital is
       <a href="/wiki/Dakar" title="Dakar">
        Dakar
       </a>
       . It is the westernmost country in the mainland of the
       <a href="/wiki/Old_World" title="Old World">
        Old World
       </a>
       , or
       <a href="/wiki/Afro-Eurasia" title="Afro-Eurasia">
        Afro-Eurasia
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and owes its name to the
       <a href="/wiki/Senegal_River" title="Senegal River">
        Senegal River
       </a>
       , which borders it to the east and north. The name "Senegal" comes from the
       <a href="/wiki/Wolof_language" title="Wolof language">
        Wolof
       </a>
       "Sunuu Gaal", which means "Our Boat". Senegal covers a land area of almost 197,000 square kilometres (76,000 sq mi) and has an estimated population of about 15 million.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The climate is
       <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">
        Sahelian
       </a>
       , but there is a
       <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">
        rainy season
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cultures_and_influences">
        Cultures and influences
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Cultures and influences">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           needs additional citations for
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            verification
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit">
            improve this article
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (April 2017)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The territory of modern Senegal has been inhabited by various ethnic groups since
       <a href="/wiki/Prehistory" title="Prehistory">
        prehistory
       </a>
       . Organized kingdoms emerged around the seventh century, and parts of the country were ruled by prominent regional empires such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Jolof_Empire" title="Jolof Empire">
        Jolof Empire
       </a>
       . The present state of Senegal has its roots in European colonialism, which began during the mid-15th century, when various European powers began competing for trade in the area. The establishment of coastal trading posts gradually led to control of the mainland, culminating in French rule of the area by the 19th century, albeit amid much local resistance. Senegal peacefully attained independence from France in 1960, and has since been among the more politically stable countries in Africa.
      </p>
      <p>
       Senegal's economy is centered mostly on commodities and natural resources. Major industries are fish processing,
       <a href="/wiki/Phosphate" title="Phosphate">
        phosphate
       </a>
       mining, fertilizer production,
       <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">
        petroleum
       </a>
       refining, construction materials, and ship construction and repair. As in most African nations, agriculture is a major sector, with Senegal producing several important cash crops, including
       <a href="/wiki/Peanut" title="Peanut">
        peanuts
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">
        sugarcane
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">
        cotton
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Green_bean" title="Green bean">
        green beans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">
        tomatoes
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Melon" title="Melon">
        melons
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">
        mangoes
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fas_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-fas-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Owing to its relative stability, tourism and hospitality are also burgeoning sectors.
      </p>
      <p>
       A multiethnic and secular nation, Senegal is predominantly
       <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">
        Sunni Muslim
       </a>
       with
       <a href="/wiki/Sufism" title="Sufism">
        Sufi
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traditional_African_religion" title="Traditional African religion">
        animist
       </a>
       influences. French is the
       <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">
        official language
       </a>
       , although many native languages are spoken and recognized. Since April 2012 Senegal's president has been
       <a href="/wiki/Macky_Sall" title="Macky Sall">
        Macky Sall
       </a>
       . Senegal has been a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">
        Organisation internationale de la Francophonie
       </a>
       since 1970.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">
        Etymology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Etymology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Senegal is named after the
       <a href="/wiki/Senegal_River" title="Senegal River">
        Senegal River
       </a>
       , the etymology of which is contested. One popular theory (proposed by David Boilat in 1853) is that it stems from the
       <a href="/wiki/Wolof_language" title="Wolof language">
        Wolof
       </a>
       phrase
       <i>
        sunu gaal
       </i>
       , which means "our canoe" (or
       <a href="/wiki/Pirogue" title="Pirogue">
        pirogue
       </a>
       ), resulting from a miscommunication between 15th-century Portuguese sailors and Wolof fishermen. The "our canoe" theory has been popularly embraced in modern Senegal for its charm. It is frequently used in appeals to national solidarity (e.g. "we're all in the same canoe"), frequently heard in the media.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Modern historians believe the name probably refers to the
       <a href="/wiki/Sanhaja" title="Sanhaja">
        Sanhaja
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">
        Berbers
       </a>
       who lived on the northern side of the river. A competing theory is that it derives from the medieval town of "Sanghana" (also spelled as Isenghan, Asengan, Singhanah), described by the Arab geographer
       <a href="/wiki/Al-Bakri" title="Al-Bakri">
        al-Bakri
       </a>
       in 1068 as located by the mouth of the river. Some
       <a href="/wiki/Serer_people" title="Serer people">
        Serer people
       </a>
       from the south believe the river's name is derived from the compound of the
       <a href="/wiki/Serer_language" title="Serer language">
        Serer
       </a>
       term
       <i>
        Sene
       </i>
       (from Roge Sene, Supreme Deity in
       <a href="/wiki/Serer_religion" title="Serer religion">
        Serer religion
       </a>
       ) and
       <i>
        O Gal
       </i>
       (meaning "body of water").
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Senegal" title="History of Senegal">
        History of Senegal
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_and_pre-colonial_eras">
        Early and pre-colonial eras
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Early and pre-colonial eras">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Archaeological findings throughout the area indicate that Senegal was inhabited in prehistoric times and has been continuously occupied by various ethnic groups. Some kingdoms were created around the 7th century:
       <a href="/wiki/Takrur" title="Takrur">
        Takrur
       </a>
       in the 9th century,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Namandiru&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Namandiru (page does not exist)">
        Namandiru
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://wo.wikipedia.org/wiki/Namandiru" title="wo:Namandiru">
         wo
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Jolof_Empire" title="Jolof Empire">
        Jolof Empire
       </a>
       during the 13th and 14th centuries. Eastern Senegal was once part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ghana_Empire" title="Ghana Empire">
        Ghana Empire
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Islam was introduced through
       <a href="/wiki/Toucouleur_people" title="Toucouleur people">
        Toucouleur
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Soninke_people" title="Soninke people">
        Soninke
       </a>
       contact with the
       <a href="/wiki/Almoravid_dynasty" title="Almoravid dynasty">
        Almoravid dynasty
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">
        Maghreb
       </a>
       , who in turn propagated it with the help of the Almoravids, and Toucouleur allies. This movement faced resistance from ethnicities of traditional religions, the Serers in particular.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 13th and 14th centuries, the area came under the influence of the empires to the east; the Jolof Empire of Senegal was also founded during this time. In the Senegambia region, between 1300 and 1900, close to one-third of the population was
       <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Africa" title="Slavery in Africa">
        enslaved
       </a>
       , typically as a result of captives taken in warfare.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 14th century the Jolof Empire grew powerful, having united
       <a href="/wiki/Cayor" title="Cayor">
        Cayor
       </a>
       and the kingdoms of
       <a href="/wiki/Baol" title="Baol">
        Baol
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sine" title="Kingdom of Sine">
        Sine
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Saloum" title="Saloum">
        Saloum
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Waalo" title="Waalo">
        Waalo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Futa_Tooro" title="Futa Tooro">
        Futa Tooro
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Bambouk" title="Bambouk">
        Bambouk
       </a>
       . The empire was a voluntary confederacy of various states rather than an empire built on military conquest.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-charles_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-charles-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The empire was founded by Ndiadiane Ndiaye, a part
       <a href="/wiki/Serer_people" title="Serer people">
        Serer
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and part
       <a href="/wiki/Toucouleur_people" title="Toucouleur people">
        Toucouleur
       </a>
       , who was able to form a coalition with many ethnicities, but collapsed around 1549 with the defeat and killing of Lele Fouli Fak by
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Amari_Ngone_Sobel_Fall&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Amari Ngone Sobel Fall (page does not exist)">
        Amari Ngone Sobel Fall
       </a>
       <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
        (
        <a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amari_Ngone_Sobel_Fall" title="fr:Amari Ngone Sobel Fall">
         fr
        </a>
        )
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_era">
        Colonial era
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Colonial era">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In the mid-15th century, the Portuguese landed on the Senegal coastline, followed by traders representing other countries, including the French.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ross_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ross-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Various European powers—Portugal, the Netherlands, and Great Britain—competed for trade in the area from the 15th century onward. In 1677, France gained control of what had become a minor departure point in the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">
        Atlantic slave trade
       </a>
       —the island of
       <a href="/wiki/Gor%C3%A9e" title="Gorée">
        Gorée
       </a>
       next to modern Dakar, used as a base to purchase slaves from the warring chiefdoms on the mainland.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-h-net.org_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-h-net.org-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3585" data-file-width="2531" height="312" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg/220px-Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg/330px-Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg/440px-Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marchands_d%27esclaves_de_Gor%C3%A9e-Jacques_Grasset_de_Saint-Sauveur_mg_8526.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Slave traders in
         <a href="/wiki/Gor%C3%A9e" title="Gorée">
          Gorée
         </a>
         , 18th century
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       European missionaries introduced Christianity to Senegal and the
       <a href="/wiki/Casamance" title="Casamance">
        Casamance
       </a>
       in the 19th century. It was only in the 1850s that the French began to expand onto the Senegalese mainland after they abolished slavery and began promoting an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_France" title="Abolitionism in France">
        abolitionist
       </a>
       doctrine,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       adding native kingdoms like the Waalo, Cayor, Baol, and Jolof Empire. French colonists progressively invaded and took over all the kingdoms except Sine and Saloum under Governor
       <a href="/wiki/Louis_Faidherbe" title="Louis Faidherbe">
        Louis Faidherbe
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-charles_14-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-charles-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Senegalese resistance to the French expansion and curtailing of their lucrative slave trade was led in part by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lat-Dior" title="Lat-Dior">
        Lat-Dior
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Damel" title="Damel">
        Damel
       </a>
       of Cayor, and
       <a href="/wiki/Maad_a_Sinig_Kumba_Ndoffene_Famak_Joof" title="Maad a Sinig Kumba Ndoffene Famak Joof">
        Maad a Sinig Kumba Ndoffene Famak Joof
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Maad_a_Sinig" title="Maad a Sinig">
        Maad a Sinig
       </a>
       of Sine, resulting in the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Logand%C3%A8me" title="Battle of Logandème">
        Battle of Logandème
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Independence_.281960.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(1960)">
        Independence (1960)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Independence (1960)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       On 4 April 1959 Senegal and the
       <a href="/wiki/French_Sudan" title="French Sudan">
        French Sudan
       </a>
       merged to form the
       <a href="/wiki/Mali_Federation" title="Mali Federation">
        Mali Federation
       </a>
       , which became fully independent on 20 June 1960, as a result of the independence and the transfer of power agreement signed with France on 4 April 1960. Due to internal political difficulties, the Federation broke up on 20 August, when Senegal and French Sudan (renamed the Republic of
       <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">
        Mali
       </a>
       ) each proclaimed independence.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9opold_S%C3%A9dar_Senghor" title="Léopold Sédar Senghor">
        Léopold Sédar Senghor
       </a>
       was proclaimed Senegal's first president in September 1960. Senghor was a very well-read man, educated in France. He was a poet and philosopher who personally drafted the Senegalese national anthem, "Pincez tous vos koras, frappez les balafons". Pro-African, he advocated a brand of African socialism.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colonial_Saint_Louis.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="289" data-file-width="450" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Colonial_Saint_Louis.jpg/220px-Colonial_Saint_Louis.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Colonial_Saint_Louis.jpg/330px-Colonial_Saint_Louis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Colonial_Saint_Louis.jpg/440px-Colonial_Saint_Louis.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Colonial_Saint_Louis.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Colonial
         <a href="/wiki/Saint-Louis,_Senegal" title="Saint-Louis, Senegal">
          Saint Louis
         </a>
         c. 1900. Europeans and Africans on the Rue Lebon.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1980, President Senghor decided to retire from politics. The next year, he transferred power in 1981 to his hand-picked successor,
       <a href="/wiki/Abdou_Diouf" title="Abdou Diouf">
        Abdou Diouf
       </a>
       . Former prime minister
       <a href="/wiki/Mamadou_Dia" title="Mamadou Dia">
        Mamadou Dia
       </a>
       , who was Senghor's rival, ran for election in 1983 against Diouf, but lost. Senghor moved to France, where he died at the age of 96.
      </p>
      <p>
       Senegal joined with
       <a href="/wiki/The_Gambia" title="The Gambia">
        the Gambia
       </a>
       to form the nominal
       <a href="/wiki/Senegambia_Confederation" title="Senegambia Confederation">
        Senegambia Confederation
       </a>
       on 1 February 1982. However, the union was dissolved in 1989. Despite peace talks, a southern separatist group (
       <a href="/wiki/Movement_of_Democratic_Forces_of_Casamance" title="Movement of Democratic Forces of Casamance">
        Movement of Democratic Forces of Casamance
       </a>
       or MFDC) in the
       <a href="/wiki/Casamance" title="Casamance">
        Casamance
       </a>
       region has clashed sporadically with government forces since 1982 in the
       <a href="/wiki/Casamance_conflict" title="Casamance conflict">
        Casamance conflict
       </a>
       . In the early 21st century, violence has subsided and President
       <a href="/wiki/Macky_Sall" title="Macky Sall">
        Macky Sall
       </a>
       held talks with rebels in Rome in December 2012.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Abdou Diouf was president between 1981 and 2000. He encouraged broader political participation, reduced government involvement in the economy, and widened Senegal's diplomatic engagements, particularly with other developing nations. Domestic politics on occasion spilled over into street violence, border tensions, and a violent separatist movement in the southern region of the Casamance. Nevertheless, Senegal's commitment to democracy and human rights strengthened. Abdou Diouf served four terms as president.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the presidential election of 1999, opposition leader
       <a href="/wiki/Abdoulaye_Wade" title="Abdoulaye Wade">
        Abdoulaye Wade
       </a>
       defeated Diouf in an election deemed free and fair by international observers. Senegal experienced its second peaceful transition of power, and its first from one political party to another. On 30 December 2004 President Wade announced that he would sign a peace treaty with the separatist group in the Casamance region. This, however, has yet to be implemented. There was a round of talks in 2005, but the results have not yet yielded a resolution.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">
        Politics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Politics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Senegal" title="Politics of Senegal">
        Politics of Senegal
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macky_Sall_.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="868" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Macky_Sall_.jpg/170px-Macky_Sall_.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Macky_Sall_.jpg/255px-Macky_Sall_.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Macky_Sall_.jpg/340px-Macky_Sall_.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Macky_Sall_.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Macky_Sall" title="Macky Sall">
          Macky Sall
         </a>
         , President of Senegal (2012–present)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Abdoulaye_Wade_in_16-05-2007.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="801" data-file-width="577" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Abdoulaye_Wade_in_16-05-2007.jpg/170px-Abdoulaye_Wade_in_16-05-2007.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Abdoulaye_Wade_in_16-05-2007.jpg/255px-Abdoulaye_Wade_in_16-05-2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Abdoulaye_Wade_in_16-05-2007.jpg/340px-Abdoulaye_Wade_in_16-05-2007.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Abdoulaye_Wade_in_16-05-2007.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Abdoulaye_Wade" title="Abdoulaye Wade">
          Abdoulaye Wade
         </a>
         , President of Senegal (2000–2012)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Senegal is a republic with a presidency; the president is
       <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Senegal" title="Elections in Senegal">
        elected
       </a>
       every five years as of 2001, previously being seven years, by adult voters. The first president,
       <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9opold_S%C3%A9dar_Senghor" title="Léopold Sédar Senghor">
        Léopold Sédar Senghor
       </a>
       , was a poet and writer, and was the first African elected to the
       <i>
        Académie française
       </i>
       . Senegal's second president,
       <a href="/wiki/Abdou_Diouf" title="Abdou Diouf">
        Abdou Diouf
       </a>
       , later served as general secretary of the
       <i>
        Organisation de la Francophonie
       </i>
       . The third president was
       <a href="/wiki/Abdoulaye_Wade" title="Abdoulaye Wade">
        Abdoulaye Wade
       </a>
       , a lawyer. The current president is
       <a href="/wiki/Macky_Sall" title="Macky Sall">
        Macky Sall
       </a>
       , elected in March 2012.
      </p>
      <p>
       Senegal has more than 80 political parties. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unicameral" title="Unicameral">
        unicameral
       </a>
       parliament consists of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Senegal" title="National Assembly of Senegal">
        National Assembly
       </a>
       , which has 150 seats (a
       <a href="/wiki/Senate_(Senegal)" title="Senate (Senegal)">
        Senate
       </a>
       was in place from 1999 to 2001 and 2007 to 2012).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       An independent judiciary also exists in Senegal. The nation's highest courts that deal with business issues are the constitutional council and the court of justice, members of which are named by the president.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">
        Political culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Political culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Currently, Senegal has a quasi-democratic political culture, one of the more successful post-colonial democratic transitions in Africa. Local administrators are appointed and held accountable by the president.
       <a href="/wiki/Marabout" title="Marabout">
        Marabouts
       </a>
       , religious leaders of the various
       <a href="/wiki/Muslim_brotherhoods_of_Senegal" title="Muslim brotherhoods of Senegal">
        Muslim brotherhoods of Senegal
       </a>
       , have also exercised a strong political influence in the country especially during Wade's presidency. In 2009,
       <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">
        Freedom House
       </a>
       downgraded Senegal's status from "Free" to "Partially Free", based on increased centralisation of power in the executive. However, it has since recovered its Free status by 2014.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2008, Senegal finished in 12th position on the
       <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Index_of_African_Governance" title="Ibrahim Index of African Governance">
        Ibrahim Index of African Governance
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibrahim_index_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ibrahim_index-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Ibrahim Index is a comprehensive measure of African governance (limited to
       <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">
        sub-Saharan Africa
       </a>
       until 2008), based on a number of different variables which reflect the success with which governments deliver essential political goods to their citizens. When the Northern African countries were added to the index in 2009, Senegal's 2008 position was retroactively downgraded to 15th place (with Tunisia, Egypt and Morocco placing themselves ahead of Senegal). As of 2012
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , Senegal's rank in the Ibrahim Index has decreased another point to 16 out of 52 African countries.
      </p>
      <p>
       On 22 February 2011, Senegal reportedly severed diplomatic ties with
       <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">
        Iran
       </a>
       , saying it supplied rebels with weapons which killed Senegalese troops in the
       <a href="/wiki/Casamance_conflict" title="Casamance conflict">
        Casamance conflict
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Senegalese_presidential_election,_2012" title="Senegalese presidential election, 2012">
        2012 presidential election
       </a>
       was controversial due to President Wade's candidacy, as the opposition argued he should not be considered eligible to run again. Several youth opposition movements, including M23 and
       <a href="/wiki/Y%27en_a_Marre" title="Y'en a Marre">
        Y'en a Marre
       </a>
       , emerged in June 2011. In the end, Macky Sall of the
       <a href="/wiki/Alliance_for_the_Republic_(Senegal)" title="Alliance for the Republic (Senegal)">
        Alliance for the Republic
       </a>
       won, and Wade conceded the election to Sall. This peaceful and democratic transition was hailed by many foreign observers, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        EU
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as a show of "maturity".
      </p>
      <p>
       On 19 September 2012, lawmakers voted to do away with the Senate to save an estimated $15 million.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">
        Administrative divisions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Senegal,_administrative_divisions_in_colour_2.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="930" data-file-width="1265" height="331" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Senegal%2C_administrative_divisions_in_colour_2.svg/450px-Senegal%2C_administrative_divisions_in_colour_2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Senegal%2C_administrative_divisions_in_colour_2.svg/675px-Senegal%2C_administrative_divisions_in_colour_2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Senegal%2C_administrative_divisions_in_colour_2.svg/900px-Senegal%2C_administrative_divisions_in_colour_2.svg.png 2x" width="450"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Senegal,_administrative_divisions_in_colour_2.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Regions of Senegal
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Senegal" title="Regions of Senegal">
        Regions of Senegal
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_Senegal" title="Departments of Senegal">
        Departments of Senegal
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Arrondissements_of_Senegal" title="Arrondissements of Senegal">
        Arrondissements of Senegal
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_Senegal" title="Communes of Senegal">
        Communes of Senegal
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Senegal is subdivided into 14 regions,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       each administered by a
       <i>
        Conseil Régional
       </i>
       (Regional Council) elected by population weight at the
       <i>
        Arrondissement
       </i>
       level. The country is further subdivided by 45
       <i>
        Départements
       </i>
       , 113
       <i>
        Arrondissements
       </i>
       (neither of which have administrative function) and by
       <i>
        Collectivités Locales
       </i>
       , which elect administrative officers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Regional capitals have the same name as their respective regions:
      </p>
      <div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
       <ul>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Dakar_Region" title="Dakar Region">
          Dakar
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Diourbel_Region" title="Diourbel Region">
          Diourbel
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Fatick_Region" title="Fatick Region">
          Fatick
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Kaffrine_Region" title="Kaffrine Region">
          Kaffrine
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Kaolack_Region" title="Kaolack Region">
          Kaolack
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/K%C3%A9dougou_Region" title="Kédougou Region">
          Kédougou
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Kolda_Region" title="Kolda Region">
          Kolda
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Louga_Region" title="Louga Region">
          Louga
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Matam_Region" title="Matam Region">
          Matam
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Saint-Louis_Region" title="Saint-Louis Region">
          Saint-Louis
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9dhiou_Region" title="Sédhiou Region">
          Sédhiou
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Tambacounda_Region" title="Tambacounda Region">
          Tambacounda
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Thi%C3%A8s_Region" title="Thiès Region">
          Thiès
         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a href="/wiki/Ziguinchor_Region" title="Ziguinchor Region">
          Ziguinchor
         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">
        Foreign relations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Senegal" title="Foreign relations of Senegal">
        Foreign relations of Senegal
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Senegal has a high profile in many international organizations and was a member of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council" title="UN Security Council">
        UN Security Council
       </a>
       in 1988–89 and 2015–2016. It was elected to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Commission_on_Human_Rights" title="UN Commission on Human Rights">
        UN Commission on Human Rights
       </a>
       in 1997. Friendly to the West, especially to France and to the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       , Senegal also is a vigorous proponent of more assistance from developed countries to the
       <a href="/wiki/Third_World" title="Third World">
        Third World
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Senegal enjoys mostly cordial relations with its neighbors. In spite of clear progress on other fronts with
       <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">
        Mauritania
       </a>
       (border security, resource management, economic integration, etc.), there remains the problem of an estimated 30,000 Afro-Mauritanian refugees living in Senegal.
      </p>
      <p>
       Senegal is part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">
        Economic Community of West African States
       </a>
       (ECOWAS). Integrated with the main bodies of the international community, Senegal is also a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">
        African Union
       </a>
       (AU) and the
       <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Sahel-Saharan_States" title="Community of Sahel-Saharan States">
        Community of Sahel-Saharan States
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Military">
        Military
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Military">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Senegal" title="Military of Senegal">
        Military of Senegal
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Landmine_warning_sign_near_Ziguinchor,_Senegal.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2865" data-file-width="4326" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Landmine_warning_sign_near_Ziguinchor%2C_Senegal.jpg/220px-Landmine_warning_sign_near_Ziguinchor%2C_Senegal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Landmine_warning_sign_near_Ziguinchor%2C_Senegal.jpg/330px-Landmine_warning_sign_near_Ziguinchor%2C_Senegal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Landmine_warning_sign_near_Ziguinchor%2C_Senegal.jpg/440px-Landmine_warning_sign_near_Ziguinchor%2C_Senegal.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Landmine_warning_sign_near_Ziguinchor,_Senegal.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Land mines were widely used in the
         <a href="/wiki/Casamance_conflict" title="Casamance conflict">
          Casamance conflict
         </a>
         between separatist rebels and the central government.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Senegalese armed forces consist of about 19,000 personnel in the army,
       <a href="/wiki/Senegalese_Air_Force" title="Senegalese Air Force">
        air force
       </a>
       , navy, and gendarmerie. The Senegalese military force receives most of its training, equipment, and support from France and the United States. Germany also provides support but on a smaller scale.
      </p>
      <p>
       Military noninterference in political affairs has contributed to Senegal's stability since independence. Senegal has participated in many international and regional peacekeeping missions. Most recently, in 2000, Senegal sent a battalion to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of Congo">
        Democratic Republic of Congo
       </a>
       to participate in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MONUC" title="MONUC">
        MONUC
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        United Nations
       </a>
       peacekeeping mission, and agreed to deploy a United States-trained battalion to
       <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">
        Sierra Leone
       </a>
       to participate in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNAMSIL" title="UNAMSIL">
        UNAMSIL
       </a>
       , another UN peacekeeping mission.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2015, Senegal participated in the Saudi Arabian-led
       <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen">
        military intervention in Yemen
       </a>
       against the
       <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">
        Shia
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Houthis" title="Houthis">
        Houthis
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Law">
        Law
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Law">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Senegal is a secular state, as defined in its Constitution.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution_of_Senegal_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Constitution_of_Senegal-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       To fight corruption, the government has created the National Anti-Corruption Office (OFNAC) and the Commission of Restitution and Recovery of Illegally Acquired Assets. According to Business Anti-Corruption Portal, President Sall created the OFNAC to replace the Commission Nationale de Lutte Contre la non Transparence, la Corruption et la Concussion (CNLCC). It is said that the OFNAC represents a more effective tool for fighting corruption than the CNLCC established under former President Wade.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The mission of OFNAC is to fight corruption, embezzlement of public funds and fraud. OFNAC has the power of self-referral (own initiative investigation). OFNAC is composed of twelve members appointed by decree.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Senegal" title="LGBT rights in Senegal">
        Homosexuality
       </a>
       is illegal in Senegal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to 2013 survey by the
       <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">
        Pew Research Center
       </a>
       , 96% of Senegalese believe that homosexuality should not be accepted by society.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pewglobal.org_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-pewglobal.org-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Senegal" title="Geography of Senegal">
        Geography of Senegal
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Senegal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1900" data-file-width="1900" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Senegal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Senegal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Senegal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Senegal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Senegal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Senegal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Senegal_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Senegal map of Köppen climate classification
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Casamance_landscape.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="389" data-file-width="583" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Casamance_landscape.jpg/220px-Casamance_landscape.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Casamance_landscape.jpg/330px-Casamance_landscape.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Casamance_landscape.jpg/440px-Casamance_landscape.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Casamance_landscape.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Landscape of
         <a href="/wiki/Casamance" title="Casamance">
          Casamance
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Senegal is located on the west of the African continent. It lies between latitudes
       <a href="/wiki/12th_parallel_north" title="12th parallel north">
        12°
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/17th_parallel_north" title="17th parallel north">
        17°N
       </a>
       , and longitudes
       <a href="/wiki/11th_meridian_west" title="11th meridian west">
        11°
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/18th_meridian_west" title="18th meridian west">
        18°W
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Senegal is externally bounded by the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">
        Atlantic Ocean
       </a>
       to the west,
       <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">
        Mauritania
       </a>
       to the north,
       <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">
        Mali
       </a>
       to the east, and
       <a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">
        Guinea
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">
        Guinea-Bissau
       </a>
       to the south; internally it almost completely surrounds
       <a href="/wiki/The_Gambia" title="The Gambia">
        The Gambia
       </a>
       , namely on the north, east and south, except for Gambia's short Atlantic coastline.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Senegalese landscape consists mainly of the rolling sandy plains of the western
       <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">
        Sahel
       </a>
       which rise to foothills in the southeast. Here is also found Senegal's highest point, an otherwise unnamed feature 2.7 km southeast of
       <a href="/wiki/Nepen_Diakha" title="Nepen Diakha">
        Nepen Diakha
       </a>
       at 648 m (2,126 ft).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The northern border is formed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Senegal_River" title="Senegal River">
        Senegal River
       </a>
       ; other rivers include the
       <a href="/wiki/Gambia_River" title="Gambia River">
        Gambia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Casamance_River" title="Casamance River">
        Casamance Rivers
       </a>
       . The capital Dakar lies on the
       <a href="/wiki/Cap-Vert" title="Cap-Vert">
        Cap-Vert
       </a>
       peninsula, the westernmost point of continental Africa.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">
        Cape Verde
       </a>
       islands lie some 560 kilometres (350 mi) off the Senegalese coast, but Cap-Vert ("Cape Green") is a maritime placemark, set at the foot of "Les Mammelles", a 105-metre (344 ft) cliff resting at one end of the Cap-Vert peninsula onto which is settled Senegal's capital Dakar, and 1 kilometre (0.6 mi) south of the "Pointe des Almadies", the westernmost point in Africa.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Climate_of_Senegal" title="Climate of Senegal">
        Climate of Senegal
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ngor_Beach.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2606" data-file-width="3475" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Ngor_Beach.jpg/220px-Ngor_Beach.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Ngor_Beach.jpg/330px-Ngor_Beach.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Ngor_Beach.jpg/440px-Ngor_Beach.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ngor_Beach.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Beach at N'Gor
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Senegal has a
       <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">
        tropical climate
       </a>
       with pleasant heat throughout the year with well-defined dry and humid seasons that result from northeast winter winds and southwest summer winds. The dry season (December to April) is dominated by hot, dry,
       <a href="/wiki/Harmattan" title="Harmattan">
        harmattan
       </a>
       wind.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_1-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Dakar's annual rainfall of about 600 mm (24 in) occurs between June and October when maximum temperatures average 30 °C (86.0 °F) and minimums 24.2 °C (75.6 °F); December to February maximum temperatures average 25.7 °C (78.3 °F) and minimums 18 °C (64.4 °F).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Interior temperatures are higher than along the coast (for example, average daily temperatures in Kaolack and Tambacounda for May are 30 °C (86.0 °F) and 32.7 °C (90.9 °F) respectively, compared to Dakar's 23.2 °C (73.8 °F) ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and rainfall increases substantially farther south, exceeding 1,500 mm (59.1 in) annually in some areas.
      </p>
      <p>
       In Tambacounda in the far interior, particularly on the border of Mali where desert begins, temperatures can reach as high as 54 °C (129.2 °F). The northernmost part of the country has a near
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_desert_climate" title="Hot desert climate">
        hot desert climate
       </a>
       , the central part has a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_semi-arid_climate" title="Hot semi-arid climate">
        hot semi-arid climate
       </a>
       and the southernmost part has a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_wet_and_dry_climate" title="Tropical wet and dry climate">
        tropical wet and dry climate
       </a>
       . Senegal is mainly a sunny and dry country.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Senegal" title="Economy of Senegal">
        Economy of Senegal
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Senegal_Export_Treemap.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="667" data-file-width="854" height="273" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Senegal_Export_Treemap.png/350px-Senegal_Export_Treemap.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Senegal_Export_Treemap.png/525px-Senegal_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Senegal_Export_Treemap.png/700px-Senegal_Export_Treemap.png 2x" width="350"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Senegal_Export_Treemap.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A proportional representation of Senegal's exports
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After its economy contracted by 2.1% in 1993, Senegal instituted a major economic reform program with the support of international donors. This reform began with a 50 percent devaluation of the country's currency (the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CFAF" title="CFAF">
        CFA franc
       </a>
       ). Government price controls and subsidies were also dismantled. As a result, Senegal's inflation went down, investment went up, and the gross domestic product rose approximately 5% a year between 1995 and 2001.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_1-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The main industries include
       <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">
        food processing
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">
        mining
       </a>
       , cement,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Artificial_fertilizer" title="Artificial fertilizer">
        artificial fertilizer
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">
        chemicals
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Textile_industry" title="Textile industry">
        textiles
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Refining" title="Refining">
        refining
       </a>
       imported petroleum, and
       <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Senegal" title="Tourism in Senegal">
        tourism
       </a>
       . Exports include fish, chemicals, cotton, fabrics,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bambara_groundnut" title="Bambara groundnut">
        groundnuts
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Calcium_phosphate" title="Calcium phosphate">
        calcium phosphate
       </a>
       . The principal foreign market is India with 26.7% of exports (as of 1998). Other foreign markets include the United States, Italy and the United Kingdom.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20130513-DSC_8564_(8750149526).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4928" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/20130513-DSC_8564_%288750149526%29.jpg/220px-20130513-DSC_8564_%288750149526%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/20130513-DSC_8564_%288750149526%29.jpg/330px-20130513-DSC_8564_%288750149526%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/20130513-DSC_8564_%288750149526%29.jpg/440px-20130513-DSC_8564_%288750149526%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:20130513-DSC_8564_(8750149526).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Fishing boats in Dakar
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Senegal has a 12-nautical-mile (22 km; 14 mi) exclusive fishing zone that has been regularly breached in recent years (as of 2014
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ). It has been estimated that the country's fishermen lose 300,000 tonnes of fish each year to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Illegal_fishing" title="Illegal fishing">
        illegal fishing
       </a>
       . The Senegalese government have tried to control the illegal fishing which is conducted by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fishing_trawlers" title="Fishing trawlers">
        fishing trawlers
       </a>
       , some of which are registered in
       <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
        Russia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">
        Mauritania
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">
        Belize
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">
        Ukraine
       </a>
       . In January 2014, a Russian trawler, Oleg Naydenov, was seized by Senegalese authorities close to the maritime border with
       <a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">
        Guinea-Bissau
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As a member of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_African_Economic_and_Monetary_Union" title="West African Economic and Monetary Union">
        West African Economic and Monetary Union
       </a>
       (WAEMU), Senegal is working toward greater regional integration with a unified external
       <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">
        tariff
       </a>
       . Senegal is also a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/OHADA" title="OHADA">
        Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ohada.com_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ohada.com-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Senegal achieved full Internet connectivity in 1996, creating a mini-boom in information technology-based services. Private activity now accounts for 82 percent of its GDP. On the negative side, Senegal faces deep-seated urban problems of chronic high unemployment,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Income_disparity" title="Income disparity">
        socioeconomic disparity
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Juvenile_delinquency" title="Juvenile delinquency">
        juvenile delinquency
       </a>
       , and drug addiction.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Senegal is a major recipient of international development assistance. Donors include the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Agency_for_International_Development" title="United States Agency for International Development">
        United States Agency for International Development
       </a>
       (USAID), Japan, France and China. Over 3,000
       <a href="/wiki/Peace_Corps" title="Peace Corps">
        Peace Corps
       </a>
       Volunteers have served in Senegal since 1963.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pcsenegal.org_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-pcsenegal.org-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Demographics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Senegal-demography2004.gif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="623" data-file-width="911" height="308" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Senegal-demography2004.gif/450px-Senegal-demography2004.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Senegal-demography2004.gif/675px-Senegal-demography2004.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Senegal-demography2004.gif/900px-Senegal-demography2004.gif 2x" width="450"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Senegal-demography2004.gif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Senegal's population from 1962 to 2004
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Senegal" title="Demographics of Senegal">
        Demographics of Senegal
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Senegal has a population of around 15.4 million
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , about 42 percent of whom live in rural areas. Density in these areas varies from about 77 inhabitants per square kilometre (200/sq mi) in the west-central region to 2 per square kilometre (5.2/sq mi) in the arid eastern section.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">
        Ethnic groups
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Senegal" title="Ethnic groups in Senegal">
        Ethnic groups in Senegal
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Senegal has a wide variety of
       <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">
        ethnic groups
       </a>
       and, as in most West African countries, several languages are widely spoken. The
       <a href="/wiki/Wolof_people" title="Wolof people">
        Wolof
       </a>
       are the largest single ethnic group in Senegal at 43 percent; the
       <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">
        Fula
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Toucouleur_people" title="Toucouleur people">
        Toucouleur
       </a>
       (also known as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Halpulaar" title="Halpulaar">
        Halpulaar
       </a>
       'en, literally "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pulaar" title="Pulaar">
        Pulaar
       </a>
       -speakers") (24%) are the second biggest group, followed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Serer_people" title="Serer people">
        Serer
       </a>
       (14.7%),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       then others such as
       <a href="/wiki/Jola_people" title="Jola people">
        Jola
       </a>
       (4%),
       <a href="/wiki/Mandinka_people" title="Mandinka people">
        Mandinka
       </a>
       (3%),
       <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">
        Maures
       </a>
       or (Naarkajors),
       <a href="/wiki/Soninke_people" title="Soninke people">
        Soninke
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bassari_people" title="Bassari people">
        Bassari
       </a>
       and many smaller communities (9%). (See also the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bedick" title="Bedick">
        Bedick
       </a>
       ethnic group.)
      </p>
      <p>
       About 50,000 Europeans (mostly French) and
       <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people_in_Senegal" title="Lebanese people in Senegal">
        Lebanese
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as well as smaller numbers of Mauritanians and
       <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
        Moroccans
       </a>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       reside in Senegal, mainly in the cities and some retirees who reside in the resort towns around Mbour. The majority of Lebanese work in commerce.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The country experienced a wave of immigration from France in the decades between World War II and Senegalese independence; most of these French people purchased homes in Dakar or other major urban centers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mercier_48-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mercier-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Also located primarily in urban settings are small
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vietnamese_community_in_Senegal" title="Vietnamese community in Senegal">
        Vietnamese communities
       </a>
       as well as a growing number of
       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people_in_Senegal" title="Chinese people in Senegal">
        Chinese immigrant traders
       </a>
       , each numbering perhaps a few hundred people.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VOA_49-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-VOA-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SCMP_50-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-SCMP-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are also tens of thousands of
       <a href="/wiki/Mauritanians_in_Senegal" title="Mauritanians in Senegal">
        Mauritanian refugees in Senegal
       </a>
       , primarily in the country's north.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the
       <i>
        World Refugee Survey 2008
       </i>
       , published by the U.S. Committee for Refugees and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Immigrants" title="Immigrants">
        Immigrants
       </a>
       , Senegal has a population of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Refugees" title="Refugees">
        refugees
       </a>
       and asylum seekers numbering approximately 23,800 in 2007. The majority of this population (20,200) is from
       <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">
        Mauritania
       </a>
       . Refugees live in N'dioum, Dodel, and small settlements along the
       <a href="/wiki/Senegal_River" title="Senegal River">
        Senegal River
       </a>
       valley.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Refugee_Survey_2008_52-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-World_Refugee_Survey_2008-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">
        Languages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Languages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Senegal" title="Languages of Senegal">
        Languages of Senegal
       </a>
      </div>
