      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PICT5483.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/PICT5483.JPG/220px-PICT5483.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/PICT5483.JPG/330px-PICT5483.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/PICT5483.JPG/440px-PICT5483.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PICT5483.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A street market in
         <a href="/wiki/Malem_Hodar_Department" title="Malem Hodar Department">
          Malem-Hodar
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       French is the
       <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">
        official language
       </a>
       , spoken at least by all those who enjoyed several years in the educational system that is of French origin (Koranic schools are even more popular, but Arabic is not widely spoken outside of the context of recitation). Most people also speak their own ethnic language while, especially in Dakar,
       <a href="/wiki/Wolof_language" title="Wolof language">
        Wolof
       </a>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">
        lingua franca
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pulaar" title="Pulaar">
        Pulaar
       </a>
       is spoken by the Fulas and Toucouleur. The
       <a href="/wiki/Serer_language" title="Serer language">
        Serer language
       </a>
       is widely spoken by both Serers and non-Serers (including President Sall, whose wife is Serer); so are the
       <a href="/wiki/Cangin_languages" title="Cangin languages">
        Cangin languages
       </a>
       , whose speakers are ethnically Serers.
       <a href="/wiki/Jola_languages" title="Jola languages">
        Jola languages
       </a>
       are widely spoken in the
       <a href="/wiki/Casamance" title="Casamance">
        Casamance
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Several of the Senegalese languages have the legal status of "
       <a href="/wiki/National_language" title="National language">
        national languages
       </a>
       ":
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balanta-Ganja_language" title="Balanta-Ganja language">
        Balanta-Ganja
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hassaniya_Arabic" title="Hassaniya Arabic">
        Hassaniya Arabic
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jola-Fonyi_language" title="Jola-Fonyi language">
        Jola-Fonyi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mandinka_language" title="Mandinka language">
        Mandinka
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mandjak_language" title="Mandjak language">
        Mandjak
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mankanya_language" title="Mankanya language">
        Mankanya
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Noon_language" title="Noon language">
        Noon
       </a>
       (Serer-Noon),
       <a href="/wiki/Pulaar_language" title="Pulaar language">
        Pulaar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Serer_language" title="Serer language">
        Serer
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Soninke_language" title="Soninke language">
        Soninke
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Wolof_language" title="Wolof language">
        Wolof
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Portuguese_based_creole_languages&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Portuguese based creole languages (page does not exist)">
        Portuguese Creole
       </a>
       , locally known as Portuguese, is a prominent minority language in
       <a href="/wiki/Ziguinchor" title="Ziguinchor">
        Ziguinchor
       </a>
       , regional capital of the
       <a href="/wiki/Casamance" title="Casamance">
        Casamance
       </a>
       , spoken by local Portuguese creoles and immigrants from Guinea-Bissau. The local Cape Verdean community speak a similar Portuguese creole,
       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verdean_Creole" title="Cape Verdean Creole">
        Cape Verdean Creole
       </a>
       , and standard Portuguese. Portuguese was introduced in Senegal's secondary education in 1961 in Dakar by the country's first president,
       <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9opold_S%C3%A9dar_Senghor" title="Léopold Sédar Senghor">
        Léopold Sédar Senghor
       </a>
       . It is currently available in most of Senegal and in higher education. It is especially prevalent in Casamance as it relates with the local cultural identity.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dakar_Roofs_-_Beach_%26_Ocean_(5651584098).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2574" data-file-width="3445" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Dakar_Roofs_-_Beach_%26_Ocean_%285651584098%29.jpg/220px-Dakar_Roofs_-_Beach_%26_Ocean_%285651584098%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Dakar_Roofs_-_Beach_%26_Ocean_%285651584098%29.jpg/330px-Dakar_Roofs_-_Beach_%26_Ocean_%285651584098%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Dakar_Roofs_-_Beach_%26_Ocean_%285651584098%29.jpg/440px-Dakar_Roofs_-_Beach_%26_Ocean_%285651584098%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dakar_Roofs_-_Beach_%26_Ocean_(5651584098).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Aerial view of Yoff Commune, Dakar
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       French is the only official language in the country, but a backlash in the form of a rising Senegalese linguistic nationalist movement supports the integration of Wolof, the common vernacular language of the country, into the national constitution.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Senegalese regions of Dakar, Diourbel, Fatick, Kaffrine, Kaolack, Kedougou, Kolda, Louga, Matam, Saint-Louis, Sedhiou, Tambacounda, Thies and Ziguinchor are members of the International Association of Francophone regions
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities">
        Largest cities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Largest cities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Senegal" title="List of cities in Senegal">
        List of cities in Senegal
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Senegal's capital of Dakar is by far the largest city in Senegal, with over two million residents.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANSD-population_56-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ANSD-population-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The second most populous city is
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Touba,_Senegal" title="Touba, Senegal">
        Touba
       </a>
       , a
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">
         de jure
        </a>
        communaute rurale
       </i>
       (rural community), with half a million.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANSD-population_56-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ANSD-population-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CitiesinSenegal_57-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CitiesinSenegal-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS">
          <span title="per WP:CIRCULAR (December 2017)">
           better source needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <br/>
      </p>

         </a>
        </td>
        <td style="text-align:right;">
         78 800
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">
         10
        </td>
        <td style="text-align:left;">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mbak%C3%A9" title="Mbaké">
          Mbaké
         </a>
        </td>
        <td style="text-align:left;">
         <a href="/wiki/Diourbel_Region" title="Diourbel Region">
          Diourbel
         </a>
        </td>
        <td style="text-align:right;">
         74 100
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
        Religion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Religion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright" style="">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">
        <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">
         <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:Yellow">
         </div>
         <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 1589.4544843868px; border-left-color:DodgerBlue">
         </div>
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue">
         </div>
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue">
         </div>
         <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 181.89932472811px; border-left-color:MediumSeaGreen">
         </div>
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:MediumSeaGreen">
         </div>
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:MediumSeaGreen">
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <p>
          Religion in Senegal (2013)
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
           <a href="#cite_note-58">
            [58]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </p>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:MediumSeaGreen; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
           Islam
          </a>
          (92%)
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
           Christianity
          </a>
          (mostly Roman Catholicism) (7%)
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Yellow; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traditional_African_religion" title="Traditional African religion">
           Traditional African religion
          </a>
          and others (1%)
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Senegal" title="Religion in Senegal">
        Religion in Senegal
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Senegal is a secular state.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution_of_Senegal_33-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Constitution_of_Senegal-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Senegal" title="Islam in Senegal">
        Islam
       </a>
       is the predominant religion in the country, practiced by approximately 94% of the country's population; the Christian community, at 5% of the population, are mostly
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">
        Roman Catholics
       </a>
       but there are still diverse
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">
        Protestant
       </a>
       denominations. One percent have
       <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">
        animist
       </a>
       beliefs, particularly in the southeastern region of the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_1-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some
       <a href="/wiki/Serer_people" title="Serer people">
        Serer people
       </a>
       follow the
       <a href="/wiki/Serer_religion" title="Serer religion">
        Serer religion
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Touba_moschee.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Touba_moschee.jpg/220px-Touba_moschee.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Touba_moschee.jpg/330px-Touba_moschee.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Touba_moschee.jpg/440px-Touba_moschee.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Touba_moschee.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Great_Mosque_of_Touba" title="Great Mosque of Touba">
          Great Mosque of Touba
         </a>
         ; home of the
         <a href="/wiki/Mouride" title="Mouride">
          Mouride
         </a>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sufi" title="Sufi">
          Sufi
         </a>
         brotherhood, it is also one of the finest examples of
         <a href="/wiki/Islamic_architecture" title="Islamic architecture">
          Islamic architecture
         </a>
         in Africa.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dakar_cathedrale.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1365" data-file-width="2048" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Dakar_cathedrale.jpg/220px-Dakar_cathedrale.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Dakar_cathedrale.jpg/330px-Dakar_cathedrale.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Dakar_cathedrale.jpg/440px-Dakar_cathedrale.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dakar_cathedrale.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Dakar" title="Dakar">
          Dakar
         </a>
         Cathedral
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Majority of the Muslims in Senegal are
       <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">
        Sunni
       </a>
       with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sufi" title="Sufi">
        Sufi
       </a>
       influences. Islamic communities in Senegal are generally organized around one of several Islamic
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sufi" title="Sufi">
        Sufi
       </a>
       orders or brotherhoods, headed by a
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khalif" title="Khalif">
         khalif
        </a>
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        xaliifa
       </i>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Wolof_language" title="Wolof language">
        Wolof
       </a>
       , from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
        Arabic
       </a>
       <i>
        khalīfa
       </i>
       ), who is usually a direct descendant of the group's founder. The two largest and most prominent Sufi orders in Senegal are the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tijaniyya" title="Tijaniyya">
        Tijaniyya
       </a>
       , whose largest sub-groups are based in the cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Tivaouane" title="Tivaouane">
        Tivaouane
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Kaolack" title="Kaolack">
        Kaolack
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/Mouride" title="Mouride">
        Murīdiyya (Murid)
       </a>
       , based in the city of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Touba,_Senegal" title="Touba, Senegal">
        Touba
       </a>
       . 27% are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nondenominational_Muslims" title="Nondenominational Muslims">
        nondenominational Muslims
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Halpulaar" title="Halpulaar">
        Halpulaar
       </a>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pulaar" title="Pulaar">
        Pulaar
       </a>
       -speakers), composed of
       <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">
        Fula people
       </a>
       , a widespread group found along the Sahel from Chad to Senegal, and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Toucouleur_people" title="Toucouleur people">
         Toucouleurs
        </a>
       </i>
       , represent 23.8 percent of the population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_1-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Historically, they were the first to become Muslim. Many of the
       <i>
        Toucouleurs
       </i>
       , or sedentary Halpulaar of the Senegal River Valley in the north, converted to Islam around a millennium ago and later contributed to Islam's propagation throughout Senegal. Success was gained among the Wolofs, but repulsed by the Serers.
      </p>
      <p>
       Most communities south of the Senegal River Valley, however, were not thoroughly
       <a href="/wiki/Islamization" title="Islamization">
        Islamized
       </a>
       . The Serer people stood out as one of this group, who spent over one thousand years resisting Islamization (see
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serer_history_(medieval_era_to_present)" title="Serer history (medieval era to present)">
        Serer history
       </a>
       ). Although many Serers are Christians or Muslim, their conversion to Islam in particular is very recent, who converted on their own free will rather than by force, although force had been tried centuries earlier unsuccessfully (see
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Battle_of_Fandane-Thiouthioune" title="The Battle of Fandane-Thiouthioune">
        the Battle of Fandane-Thiouthioune
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The spread of formal Quranic school (called
       <i>
        daara
       </i>
       in Wolof) during the colonial period increased largely through the effort of the Tidjâniyya. In Murid communities, which place more emphasis on the work ethic than on literary Quranic studies, the term
       <i>
        daara
       </i>
       often applies to work groups devoted to working for a religious leader. Other Islamic groups include the much older Qādiriyya order and the Senegalese
       <a href="/wiki/Layene" title="Layene">
        Laayeen
       </a>
       order, which is prominent among the coastal Lebu. Today, most Senegalese children study at
       <i>
        daara
       </i>
       s for several years, memorizing as much of the Qur'an as they can. Some of them continue their religious studies at councils (
       <i>
        majlis
       </i>
       ) or at the growing number of private Arabic schools and publicly funded Franco-Arabic schools. A modern messianic sect in Islam, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya_Muslim_Community" title="Ahmadiyya Muslim Community">
        Ahmadiyya Muslim Community
       </a>
       is also present in the country which represents approximately 1% of the Muslim population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pew_63-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-pew-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Small Roman Catholic communities are mainly found in coastal Serer,
       <a href="/wiki/Jola_people" title="Jola people">
        Jola
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mankanya_people" title="Mankanya people">
        Mankanya
       </a>
       and Balant populations, and in eastern Senegal among the Bassari and Coniagui. The Protestant churches are mainly attended by immigrants but during the second half of the 20th century Protestant churches led by Senegalese leaders from different ethnic groups have evolved. In Dakar Catholic and Protestant rites are practiced by the Lebanese, Cape Verdean, European, and American immigrant populations, and among certain Africans of other countries as well as by the Senegalese themselves. Although Islam is Senegal's majority religion, Senegal's first president,
       <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9opold_S%C3%A9dar_Senghor" title="Léopold Sédar Senghor">
        Léopold Sédar Senghor
       </a>
       , was a Catholic Serer.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Touba3.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Touba3.jpg/220px-Touba3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Touba3.jpg/330px-Touba3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Touba3.jpg/440px-Touba3.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Touba3.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Boys studying Quran,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Touba,_Senegal" title="Touba, Senegal">
          Touba
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Serer_religion" title="Serer religion">
        Serer religion
       </a>
       encompasses a belief in a supreme deity called
       <a href="/wiki/Roog" title="Roog">
        Roog
       </a>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Koox" title="Koox">
        Koox
       </a>
       among the
       <a href="/wiki/Cangin_languages" title="Cangin languages">
        Cangin
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Serer_creation_myth" title="Serer creation myth">
        Serer cosmogony
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Religious_cosmology" title="Religious cosmology">
        cosmology
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Divination" title="Divination">
        divination
       </a>
       ceremonies such as the annual
       <i>
        Xoy
       </i>
       (or
       <i>
        Khoye
       </i>
       ) ceremony precided over by the Serer
       <a href="/wiki/Saltigue" title="Saltigue">
        Saltigues
       </a>
       (high priests and priestesses).
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Senegambia" title="Senegambia">
        Senegambian
       </a>
       (both Senegal and
       <a href="/wiki/The_Gambia" title="The Gambia">
        the Gambia
       </a>
       ) Muslim festivals such as
       <i>
        Tobaski
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Gamo
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Koriteh
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Weri Kor
       </i>
       , etc.,
       <a href="/wiki/Serer_religion#Influence_in_Senegambia" title="Serer religion">
        are all borrowed words from the Serer religion
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-N.Diouf_64-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-N.Diouf-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They were ancient Serer festivals rooted in Serer religion, not Islam.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-N.Diouf_64-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-N.Diouf-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Boukout" title="Boukout">
        Boukout
       </a>
       is one of the Jola's religious ceremonies.
      </p>
      <p>
       There are small numbers of adherents of
       <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">
        Judaism
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">
        Buddhism
       </a>
       . Judaism is followed by members of several ethnic groups,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">
          <span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (October 2011)">
           who?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       while Buddhism is followed by a number of Vietnamese.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_in_Senegal" title="Bahá'í Faith in Senegal">
        Bahá'í Faith in Senegal
       </a>
       was established after
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%27Abdu%27l-Bah%C3%A1" title="'Abdu'l-Bahá">
        'Abdu'l-Bahá
       </a>
       , the son of the founder of the religion, mentioned Africa as a place that should be more broadly visited by Bahá'ís.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ToDP8_65-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ToDP8-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first Bahá'is to set foot in the territory of
       <a href="/wiki/French_West_Africa" title="French West Africa">
        French West Africa
       </a>
       that would become Senegal arrived in 1953.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hassal-egypt_66-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-hassal-egypt-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first Bahá'í
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Local_Spiritual_Assembly" title="Local Spiritual Assembly">
        Local Spiritual Assembly
       </a>
       of Senegal was elected in 1966 in
       <a href="/wiki/Dakar" title="Dakar">
        Dakar
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50th_67-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-50th-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1975 the Bahá'í community elected the first
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Spiritual_Assembly" title="National Spiritual Assembly">
        National Spiritual Assembly
       </a>
       of Senegal. The most recent estimate, by the
       <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Religion_Data_Archives" title="Association of Religion Data Archives">
        Association of Religion Data Archives
       </a>
       in a 2005 report details the population of Senegalese Bahá'ís at 22,000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WCE-05_68-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-WCE-05-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Health">
        Health
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Health">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_in_Senegal" title="Health in Senegal">
        Health in Senegal
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Life expectancy by birth is estimated to 57.5 years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANSD_69-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ANSD-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Public expenditure on health was at 2.4 percent of the GDP in 2004, whereas private expenditure was at 3.5 percent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_70-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Health expenditure was at US$72 (PPP) per capita in 2004.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_70-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The fertility rate ranged 5 to 5.3 between 2005 and 2013, with 4.1 in urban areas and 6.3 in rural areas, as official survey (6.4 in 1986 and 5.7 in 1997) point out.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There were six physicians per 100,000 persons in the early 2000s (decade).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_70-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">
        Infant mortality
       </a>
       was at 77 per 1,000 live births in 2005,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_70-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but in 2013 this figure had dropped to 47 within the first 12 months after birth.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANSD_69-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ANSD-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the past 5 years infant mortality rates of malaria have dropped. According to a 2013 UNICEF report,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNICEF2013p27_72-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-UNICEF2013p27-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       26% of women in Senegal have undergone
       <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">
        female genital mutilation
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Senegal_students.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Senegal_students.jpg/220px-Senegal_students.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Senegal_students.jpg/330px-Senegal_students.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Senegal_students.jpg/440px-Senegal_students.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Senegal_students.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Students in Senegal
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Senegal" title="Education in Senegal">
        Education in Senegal
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Articles 21 and 22 of the Constitution adopted in January 2001 guarantee access to education for all children.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_73-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ilab-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Education is compulsory and free up to the age of 16.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_73-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ilab-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Ministry of Labor has indicated that the public school system is unable to cope with the number of children that must enroll each year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ilab_73-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-ilab-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">
        Illiteracy
       </a>
       is high, particularly among women.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_70-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The net primary enrollment rate was 69 percent in 2005. Public expenditure on education was 5.4 percent of the 2002–2005 GDP.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Le_Monument_de_la_Renaissance_africaine.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1296" data-file-width="1936" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Le_Monument_de_la_Renaissance_africaine.jpg/220px-Le_Monument_de_la_Renaissance_africaine.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Le_Monument_de_la_Renaissance_africaine.jpg/330px-Le_Monument_de_la_Renaissance_africaine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Le_Monument_de_la_Renaissance_africaine.jpg/440px-Le_Monument_de_la_Renaissance_africaine.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Le_Monument_de_la_Renaissance_africaine.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/African_Renaissance_Monument" title="African Renaissance Monument">
          African Renaissance Monument
         </a>
         , built in 2010 in
         <a href="/wiki/Dakar" title="Dakar">
          Dakar
         </a>
         , is the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_statues_by_height" title="List of statues by height">
          tallest statue in Africa
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Senegal is well known for the West African tradition of storytelling, which is done by
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Griot" title="Griot">
         griots
        </a>
       </i>
       , who have kept West African history alive for thousands of years through words and music. The
       <i>
        griot
       </i>
       profession is passed down generation to generation and requires years of training and apprenticeship in genealogy, history and music.
       <i>
        Griots
       </i>
       give voice to generations of West African society.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ross_18-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ross-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/African_Renaissance_Monument" title="African Renaissance Monument">
        African Renaissance Monument
       </a>
       built in 2010 in
       <a href="/wiki/Dakar" title="Dakar">
        Dakar
       </a>
       is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_statues_by_height" title="List of statues by height">
        tallest statue in Africa
       </a>
       . Dakar also hosts a film festival, Recidak.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">
        Cuisine
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Cuisine">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Senegalese_cuisine" title="Senegalese cuisine">
        Senegalese cuisine
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Because Senegal borders the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">
        Atlantic Ocean
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fish_as_food" title="Fish as food">
        fish
       </a>
       is very important.
       <a href="/wiki/Chicken_as_food" title="Chicken as food">
        Chicken
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lamb_and_mutton" title="Lamb and mutton">
        lamb
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pea" title="Pea">
        peas
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egg_(food)" title="Egg (food)">
        eggs
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">
        beef
       </a>
       are also used in Senegalese cooking, but not
       <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">
        pork
       </a>
       , due to the nation's largely
       <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">
        Muslim
       </a>
       population.
       <a href="/wiki/Peanut" title="Peanut">
        Peanuts
       </a>
       , the primary crop of Senegal, as well as
       <a href="/wiki/Couscous" title="Couscous">
        couscous
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/White_rice" title="White rice">
        white rice
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sweet_potato" title="Sweet potato">
        sweet potatoes
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lentil" title="Lentil">
        lentils
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Black-eyed_pea" title="Black-eyed pea">
        black-eyed peas
       </a>
       and various vegetables, are also incorporated into many recipes. Meats and vegetables are typically stewed or marinated in herbs and spices, and then poured over rice or couscous, or eaten with bread.
      </p>
      <p>
       Popular fresh juices are made from
       <a href="/wiki/Hibiscus" title="Hibiscus">
        bissap
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ginger" title="Ginger">
        ginger
       </a>
       ,
       <i>
        buy
       </i>
       (pronounced 'buoy', which is the fruit of the
       <a href="/wiki/Adansonia_digitata" title="Adansonia digitata">
        baobab
       </a>
       tree, also known as "monkey bread fruit"),
       <a href="/wiki/Mango" title="Mango">
        mango
       </a>
       , or other fruit or wild trees (most famously
       <a href="/wiki/Soursop" title="Soursop">
        soursop
       </a>
       , which is called
       <i>
        corossol
       </i>
       in French). Desserts are very rich and sweet, combining native ingredients with the extravagance and style characteristic of the French impact on Senegal's culinary methods. They are often served with fresh fruit and are traditionally followed by
       <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">
        coffee
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Tea" title="Tea">
        tea
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">
        Music
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Music">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Senegal" title="Music of Senegal">
        Music of Senegal
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Solo_cissokho_DSC_0448.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2577" data-file-width="1777" height="319" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Solo_cissokho_DSC_0448.JPG/220px-Solo_cissokho_DSC_0448.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Solo_cissokho_DSC_0448.JPG/330px-Solo_cissokho_DSC_0448.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Solo_cissokho_DSC_0448.JPG/440px-Solo_cissokho_DSC_0448.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Solo_cissokho_DSC_0448.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Kora_(instrument)" title="Kora (instrument)">
          Kora
         </a>
         player from Senegal
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Senegal is known across Africa for its musical heritage, due to the popularity of
       <a href="/wiki/Mbalax" title="Mbalax">
        mbalax
       </a>
       , which originated from the Serer
       <a href="/wiki/Percussion_instrument" title="Percussion instrument">
        percussive
       </a>
       tradition especially the
       <a href="/wiki/Njuup" title="Njuup">
        Njuup
       </a>
       , it has been popularized by
       <a href="/wiki/Youssou_N%27Dour" title="Youssou N'Dour">
        Youssou N'Dour
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Omar_Pene" title="Omar Pene">
        Omar Pene
       </a>
       and others.
       <a href="/wiki/Sabar" title="Sabar">
        Sabar
       </a>
       drumming is especially popular. The sabar is mostly used in special celebrations like weddings. Another instrument, the
       <a href="/wiki/Talking_drum" title="Talking drum">
        tama
       </a>
       , is used in more ethnic groups. Other popular international renowned Senegalese musicians are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ismael_L%C3%B4" title="Ismael Lô">
        Ismael Lô
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cheikh_L%C3%B4" title="Cheikh Lô">
        Cheikh Lô
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Orchestra_Baobab" title="Orchestra Baobab">
        Orchestra Baobab
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Baaba_Maal" title="Baaba Maal">
        Baaba Maal
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Akon" title="Akon">
        Akon
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Thione_Seck" title="Thione Seck">
        Thione Seck
       </a>
       , Viviane,
       <a href="/wiki/Titi_(singer)" title="Titi (singer)">
        Titi
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Pape_Diouf" title="Pape Diouf">
        Pape Diouf
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">
        Cinema
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Cinema">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Senegal" title="Cinema of Senegal">
        Cinema of Senegal
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Media">
        Media
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Media">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Senegal" title="Media of Senegal">
        Media of Senegal
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hospitality">
        Hospitality
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Hospitality">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Hospitality, in theory, is given such importance in Senegalese culture that it is widely considered to be part of the national identity. The Wolof
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Serer_Jom_75-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Serer_Jom-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       word for hospitality is "teranga" and it is so identified with the pride of Senegal that the national football team is known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Senegal_national_football_team" title="Senegal national football team">
        Lions of Teranga
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ross_18-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-ross-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research">
          <span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (October 2011)">
           original research?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Senegalese play the sport of football.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Wrestling">
        Wrestling
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Wrestling">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Senegalese_wrestling" title="Senegalese wrestling">
        Senegalese wrestling
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Wrestling is Senegal's most popular sport
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and has become a national obsession.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It traditionally serves many young men to escape poverty and it is the only sport recognized as developed independently of Western culture.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Football">
        Football
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Football">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MurPeint-ElHadjDiouf-Dakar-S%C3%A9n%C3%A9gal.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="384" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/MurPeint-ElHadjDiouf-Dakar-S%C3%A9n%C3%A9gal.jpg/220px-MurPeint-ElHadjDiouf-Dakar-S%C3%A9n%C3%A9gal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/MurPeint-ElHadjDiouf-Dakar-S%C3%A9n%C3%A9gal.jpg/330px-MurPeint-ElHadjDiouf-Dakar-S%C3%A9n%C3%A9gal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/90/MurPeint-ElHadjDiouf-Dakar-S%C3%A9n%C3%A9gal.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MurPeint-ElHadjDiouf-Dakar-S%C3%A9n%C3%A9gal.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Painting of footballer
         <a href="/wiki/El_Hadji_Diouf" title="El Hadji Diouf">
          El Hadji Diouf
         </a>
         in Dakar
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">
        Football
       </a>
       is a popular sport in Senegal. In 2002, the team finished as runners-up at the
       <a href="/wiki/Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="Africa Cup of Nations">
        Africa Cup of Nations
       </a>
       and became one of only three African teams to ever reach the quarter-finals of the
       <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">
        FIFA World Cup
       </a>
       , defeating holders
       <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">
        France
       </a>
       in their first game. Popular players of this team included
       <a href="/wiki/El_Hadji_Diouf" title="El Hadji Diouf">
        El Hadji Diouf
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Khalilou_Fadiga" title="Khalilou Fadiga">
        Khalilou Fadiga
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Henri_Camara" title="Henri Camara">
        Henri Camara
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Papa_Bouba_Diop" title="Papa Bouba Diop">
        Papa Bouba Diop
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Salif_Diao" title="Salif Diao">
        Salif Diao
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Coly" title="Ferdinand Coly">
        Ferdinand Coly
       </a>
       all of whom played in Europe.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">
        Basketball
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Basketball">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">
        Basketball
       </a>
       is also a popular sport in Senegal. The country has traditionally been one of Africa's dominant basketball powers. The
       <a href="/wiki/Senegal_national_basketball_team" title="Senegal national basketball team">
        men's team
       </a>
       performed better than any other African nation at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2014_FIBA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIBA World Cup">
        2014 FIBA World Cup
       </a>
       , where they reached the playoffs for the first time. The
       <a href="/wiki/Senegal_women%27s_national_basketball_team" title="Senegal women's national basketball team">
        women's team
       </a>
       won 19 medals at 20
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIBA_Africa_Championship_for_Women" title="FIBA Africa Championship for Women">
        African Championships
       </a>
       , more than twice as many medals as any competitor.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2016, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NBA" title="NBA">
        NBA
       </a>
       announced the launch of an Elite's Academy in Africa, and more precisely in Senegal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Motorsport">
        Motorsport
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Senegal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Motorsport">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The country hosted the
       <a href="/wiki/Dakar_Rally" title="Dakar Rally">
        Paris–Dakar rally
       </a>
       from
       <a href="/wiki/1979_Paris%E2%80%93Dakar_Rally" title="1979 Paris–Dakar Rally">
        1979
       </a>
       until
       <a href="/wiki/2007_Dakar_Rally" title="2007 Dakar Rally">
        2007
       </a>
       . The Dakar Rally was an off-road endurance motorsport race which followed a course from Paris, France to Dakar, Senegal. The competitors used off-road vehicles to cross the difficult geography. The last race was held in 2007, before the 2008 rally was canceled a day before the event due to security concerns in
       <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">
        Mauritania
       </a>
       .
      </p>

          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <cite class="citation news">
            Baba Diop.
            <a class="external text" href="http://fr.africatime.com/senegal/articles/apres-dix-annees-dinterruption-les-recidak-nouvelles-arrivent-en-2014" rel="nofollow">
             "Après dix années d'interruption : Les RECIDAK nouvelles arrivent en 2014"
            </a>
            (in French). Africatime.
           </cite>
           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=Apr%C3%A8s+dix+ann%C3%A9es+d%27interruption+%3A+Les+RECIDAK+nouvelles+arrivent+en+2014&amp;rft.au=Baba+Diop&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Ffr.africatime.com%2Fsenegal%2Farticles%2Fapres-dix-annees-dinterruption-les-recidak-nouvelles-arrivent-en-2014&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASenegal">
            <span style="display:none;">
            </span>
           </span>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-Serer_Jom-75">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-Serer_Jom_75-0">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           The word
           <i>
            taranga
           </i>
           (hospitality),
           <i>
            jom
           </i>
           (honour), etc., are all
           <a href="/wiki/Serer_people" title="Serer people">
            Serer
           </a>
           from the
           <a href="/wiki/Serer_language" title="Serer language">
            Serer language
           </a>
           , rooted in Serer values and
           <a href="/wiki/Serer_religion" title="Serer religion">
            serer religion
           </a>
           , not Wolof. See:
           <span class="languageicon">
            (in French)
           </span>
           <a href="/wiki/Henry_Gravrand" title="Henry Gravrand">
            Gravrand, Henry
           </a>
           , "L'HERITAGE SPIRITUEL SEREER: VALEUR TRADITIONNELLE D'HIER, D'AUJOURD'HUI ET DE DEMAIN" [in] Ethiopiques, numéro 31, révue socialiste de culture négro-africaine, 3e trimestre 1982
           <a class="external autonumber" href="http://ethiopiques.refer.sn/spip.php?article895" rel="nofollow">
            [1]
           </a>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-76">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-76">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           <cite class="citation web">

            . Ohio University
